        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3032845237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10010290283464021753">The most costly expense in any business or profession isn't materials, advertising, or even labor--it's bad decision-making, yet we do audits and strategize how to minimize expenses for everything but that. What Tsipursky has written is a a guide to "continuous improvement" and "agile development" of the brain. <br/>It's no secret that even high-functioning business leaders can become overwhelmed by limitless information availability and endless competing demands. The idea that we can trust our gut i</span>
  <span id="freeText10010290283464021753" style="display:none">The most costly expense in any business or profession isn't materials, advertising, or even labor--it's bad decision-making, yet we do audits and strategize how to minimize expenses for everything but that. What Tsipursky has written is a a guide to "continuous improvement" and "agile development" of the brain. <br />It's no secret that even high-functioning business leaders can become overwhelmed by limitless information availability and endless competing demands. The idea that we can trust our gut is comforting and familiar--but Tsipursky makes a clear case that it's just not so--particularly in cases where emotions, biases, and even misinformation are involved. It's precisely in situations where rationality is most needed that it can be in shortest supply. This book shows readers how to bridge the gap between wanting to make the most informed and reliable choices and knowing how to make it so. <br />A must-read for leaders, but also anyone who wants to minimize the awful feeling of looking back with regret and wondering how we did things that in hindsight, make no rational sense. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10010290283464021753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText8849556979751430399" style="display:none">As the podcast host of Internal Control Talks, I interviewed Gleb about this book, and we had a very insightful conversation on how cognitive bias could lead decision-makers to take disastrous decisions, especially in challenging times such as now with Covid.<br />This book is a must-read for everybody as each one of us makes decisions every moment of the day.   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3032869248?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Randy Grein" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Randy Grein" href="/user/show/94313605-randy-grein">Randy Grein</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/44672788-never-go-with-your-gut">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3032869248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17286936256062558919">Like many who grew up during the space race I loved Star Trek. I loved science even more, and always tried to stick to logic and reason. 'Go with your gut' was an strategy I always rejected but even so there are always improvements to be made. Gelb's book is not just a casual read but a manual how to improve decision making. A casual read will help, but the real benefit comes from doing the exercises in each chapter. These are designed to redirect decision making to more productive strategies. N</span>
  <span id="freeText17286936256062558919" style="display:none">Like many who grew up during the space race I loved Star Trek. I loved science even more, and always tried to stick to logic and reason. 'Go with your gut' was an strategy I always rejected but even so there are always improvements to be made. Gelb's book is not just a casual read but a manual how to improve decision making. A casual read will help, but the real benefit comes from doing the exercises in each chapter. These are designed to redirect decision making to more productive strategies. None are difficult but don't neglect them - the benefit is not the 'aha! experience but in practicing those strategies until they become habit. This may take just a few minutes each or hours, but please do not skimp. New thought habits are easy to shed and you'll want to have these down solid.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17286936256062558919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3198956521" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3198956521" />
    <a title="Lis Regula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17311477-lis-regula"><img alt="Lis Regula" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548594696p2/17311477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3198956521?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lis Regula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lis Regula" href="/user/show/17311477-lis-regula">Lis Regula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3198956521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3663842705526573786">Gleb's book is a great reminder to not just 'shoot from the hip' as well as an instructional guide on how to better make decisions that are evidence based and not emotional. We all have times when we react instead of respond, and that reaction can be poorly thought out (or not thought out at all), poorly executed, or poorly communicate (or a combination of these things). Learning how to avoid common mistakes of the emotions is one great lesson of this book, and far from the only one. While this </span>
  <span id="freeText3663842705526573786" style="display:none">Gleb's book is a great reminder to not just 'shoot from the hip' as well as an instructional guide on how to better make decisions that are evidence based and not emotional. We all have times when we react instead of respond, and that reaction can be poorly thought out (or not thought out at all), poorly executed, or poorly communicate (or a combination of these things). Learning how to avoid common mistakes of the emotions is one great lesson of this book, and far from the only one. While this book seems targeted to business decision makers, it's also helpful to people living in a relationship, people who live on their own, students- pretty much anyone who has to make decisions at some point and with some regularity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3663842705526573786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fGsOs3dto5o8HlcgCwPRMcFxN/HAMHAtHHMk120Ir/XoNZnEDrObdljsuxpP2sjHTEg3bsq3xwgg1pV5h6vA5Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

The pass was intercepted and the Seahawks lost. Critics called it the dumbest play in history. But was the call really that bad? Or did Carroll actually make a great move that was ruined by bad luck?\n\nEven the best decision doesn\'t yield the best outcome every time. There\'s always an element of luck that you can\'t control, and there is always information that is hidden from view. So the key to long-term success (and avoiding worrying yourself to death) is to think in bets: How sure am I? What are the possible ways things could turn out? What decision has the highest odds of success? Did I land in the unlucky 10% on the strategy that works 90% of the time? Or is my success attributable to dumb luck rather than great decision making?\n\nAnnie Duke, a former World Series of Poker champion turned business consultant, draws on examples from business, sports, politics, and (of course) poker to share tools anyone can use to embrace uncertainty and make better decisions. For most people, it\'s difficult to say &quot;I\'m not sure&quot; in a world that values and, even, rewards the appearance of certainty. But professional poker players are comfortable with the fact that great decisions don\'t always lead to great outcomes and bad decisions don\'t always lead to bad outcomes.\n\nBy shifting your thinking from a need for certainty to a goal of accurately assessing what you know and what you don\'t, you\'ll be less vulnerable to reactive emotions, knee-jerk biases, and destructive habits in your decision making. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13200125175887217755">An internationally-recognized thought leader known as the Disaster Avoidance Expert, Dr. Gleb Tsipursky is on a mission to protect leaders from dangerous judgment errors known as cognitive biases by developing the most effective decision-making strategies. <br/><br/>He wrote several best-selling books, including Never Go With Your Gut: How Pioneering Leaders Make the Best Decisions and Avoid Business Disast</span>
  <span id="freeText13200125175887217755" style="display:none">An internationally-recognized thought leader known as the Disaster Avoidance Expert, Dr. Gleb Tsipursky is on a mission to protect leaders from dangerous judgment errors known as cognitive biases by developing the most effective decision-making strategies. <br /><br />He wrote several best-selling books, including Never Go With Your Gut: How Pioneering Leaders Make the Best Decisions and Avoid Business Disasters (Career Press, 2019), The Blindspots Between Us: How to Overcome Unconscious Cognitive Bias and Build Better Relationships (New Harbinger, 2020), and Resilience: Adapt and Plan for the New Abnormal of the COVID-19 Coronavirus Pandemic (Changemakers Books, 2020). Dr. Tsipursky’s cutting-edge thought leadership was featured in over 550 articles and 450 interviews in Fast Company, CBS News, CNBC, Entrepreneur, Time, Business Insider, Government Executive, The Chronicle of Philanthropy, Inc. Magazine, and elsewhere.<br /><br />His expertise stems from over 20 years of consulting, coaching, speaking, and training experience as CEO of Disaster Avoidance Experts. Its hundreds of clients, mid-size and large companies and nonprofits, span North America, Europe, and Australia, and include Aflac, IBM, Honda, Wells Fargo, and the World Wildlife Fund. It also comes from his strong research and teaching background in behavioral economics and cognitive neuroscience with over 15 years in academia, including 7 years as a professor at the Ohio State University. He published dozens of peer-reviewed articles in academic journals such as Behavior and Social Issues and Journal of Social and Political Psychology.<br /><br />He lives in Columbus, OH, and to avoid disaster in his personal life makes sure to spend ample time with his wife. Contact him at Gleb[at]DisasterAvoidanceExperts[dot]com, follow him on Twitter @gleb_tsipursky, Instagram @dr_gleb_tsipursky, and register for his free Wise Decision Maker Course <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://disasteravoidanceexperts.com/subscribe/">https://disasteravoidanceexperts.com/...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13200125175887217755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
